Media {#Media}
--------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Media")\]

Bogotá is home to [several television stations](/wiki/Template:Bogot%C3%A1_TV "Template:Bogotá TV") like [Canal Capital](/wiki/Canal_Capital "Canal Capital") and [Citytv](/wiki/Citytv_Bogot%C3%A1 "Citytv Bogotá") which are local stations, [Canal 13](/wiki/Canal_13_(Colombia) "Canal 13 (Colombia)") is a regional station, and is home to the national channels [Caracol TV](/wiki/Caracol_TV "Caracol TV"), [RCN TV](/wiki/RCN_TV "RCN TV"), [Canal Uno](/wiki/Canal_Uno_(Colombia) "Canal Uno (Colombia)"), [Canal Institucional](/wiki/Canal_Institucional "Canal Institucional"), and [Señal Colombia](/wiki/Se%C3%B1al_Colombia "Señal Colombia"). It has multiple satellite television services like [Telefónica](/wiki/Telef%C3%B3nica "Telefónica"), [Claro](/wiki/Claro_Americas "Claro Americas") and [DirecTV](/wiki/DirecTV "DirecTV") and several satellite dishes which offer hundreds of international channels, plus several exclusive channels for Bogotá.

In Bogotá, all the major radio networks in the country are available, in both AM and FM; 70% of the FM stations offer [RDS service](/wiki/Radio_Data_System "Radio Data System"). There are several newspapers, including *[El Tiempo](/wiki/El_Tiempo_(Colombia) "El Tiempo (Colombia)")* , *[El Espectador](/wiki/El_Espectador "El Espectador")* and *[El Nuevo Siglo](/wiki/El_Nuevo_Siglo "El Nuevo Siglo")* , plus economical dailies *La República* and *Portafolio* , tabloids *El Espacio* , *Q'Hubo* , and *Extra* . Bogotá also offers three free newspapers, two Spanish, ADN and [Publimetro](/wiki/Publimetro "Publimetro"), and one English, The Bogotá Post.  
Further information on the 1849 former newspaper: [La Voz del Pueblo](/wiki/La_Voz_del_Pueblo_(Bogot%C3%A1) "La Voz del Pueblo (Bogotá)")  

Infrastructure {#Infrastructure}
--------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Infrastructure")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Avenida_Caracas_calle_40_A_Casa_de_ladrillo.JPG/220px-Avenida_Caracas_calle_40_A_Casa_de_ladrillo.JPG)](/wiki/File:Avenida_Caracas_calle_40_A_Casa_de_ladrillo.JPG) An old house in the [Teusaquillo](/wiki/Teusaquillo "Teusaquillo") locality, near downtown Bogotá (*Estrato 4*)

Energy and sewer bills are stratified based on the location of owner's residence,^[\[94\]](#cite_note-94)^ The system is the classification of the residential properties that should receive public services.^[\[95\]](#cite_note-estrato-95)^ Although the system does not consider the income per person and the rules say that the residential real estate should stratify and not households.^[\[96\]](#cite_note-Preguntas_frecuentes_estratificación-96)^ All mayors should do the stratification of residential properties of their municipality or district.^[\[95\]](#cite_note-estrato-95)^{#cite_ref-estrato_95-1}

Bogotá's social strata have been divided as follows and have been extensively used by the government as a reference to develop social welfare programs, statistical information and to some degree for the assignment of lands.

* Estrato 1 (lowest)
* Estrato 2 (low)
* Estrato 3 (mid-low)
* Estrato 4 (mid-high)
* Estrato 5 (high)
* Estrato 6 (highest)

Transport {#Transport}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Transport")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/TransMilenio_Bogota_Map.png/220px-TransMilenio_Bogota_Map.png)](/wiki/File:TransMilenio_Bogota_Map.png) Map of the [TransMilenio](/wiki/TransMilenio "TransMilenio") system

In addition to this, the metropolis currently^\[*[when?](/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items "Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers")*\]^ has over 650 kilometers of urban bicycle paths divided among its 20 boroughs, making it the city with the largest bicycle lane system on the planet. Bogotá massive urban growth during the 20th and 21st centuries due to immigration and rapid urbanization of neighboring cities has placed a strain on the city's downtown avenues and highways, but since the creation of the Bogota Metropolitan area in 1990 significant efforts to upgrade the city's infrastructure have been undertaken, including the construction of several new avenues and boulevards, as well as the construction of the first two lines of the Bogota Metro. In recent years^\[*[when?](/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items "Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers")*\]^, the capital district has embarked on several city building projects including the expansion of the Avenida Boyaca and Autopista Norte, as well as the construction of the brand new Avenida Guayacanes, a 13-kilometer 8-lane avenue currently being constructed from scratch in the boroughs of Bosa and Kennedy, as well as the excavations for the city's second metro line.^[\[97\]](#cite_note-97)^ Private car ownership forms a major part of the congestion, in addition to taxis, buses, and commercial vehicles. Buses remain the main means of mass transit. There are two bus systems: the traditional system and the [TransMilenio](/wiki/TransMilenio "TransMilenio") BRT system. The city's administration is currently in the process of replacing and updating the entire fleet for the [TransMilenio](/wiki/TransMilenio "TransMilenio") BRT system, adopting Euro VI-standard CNG-powered buses as well as electric buses. Once completed, Bogotá will have the largest electric bus fleet in the world outside China.{#cite_ref-97}

The traditional system runs a variety of bus types, operated by several companies on normal streets and avenues: *Bus* (large buses), *Buseta* (medium size buses) and *Colectivo* (vans or minivans). The bigger buses were divided into two categories: *Ejecutivo* , which was originally to be a deluxe service and was not to carry standing passengers, and *corriente* or normal service. Since May 2008, all buses run as *corriente* services. Bogotá is a [hub](/wiki/Transportation_hub "Transportation hub") for domestic and international bus routes. The Bogotá terminal serves routes to most cities and towns in Colombia^[\[98\]](#cite_note-98)^ and is the largest in the country. There is international service to Ecuador, Peru and Venezuela.{#cite_ref-98}

The [TransMilenio](/wiki/TransMilenio "TransMilenio") system was created during [Enrique Peñalosa](/wiki/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1alosa "Enrique Peñalosa")'s mayoral term,^[\[99\]](#cite_note-99)^ and is a form of [bus rapid transit](/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit "Bus rapid transit") that has been deployed as a measure to compensate for the lack of a subway or rail system. TransMilenio combines articulated buses that operate on dedicated bus roads (busways) and smaller buses (feeders) that operate in residential areas, bringing passengers to the main grid. TransMilenio's main routes are: Caracas Avenue, Northern Highway (*[Autopista Norte](/wiki/Autopista_Norte "Autopista Norte")* ), 80th Street, Americas Avenue, Jiménez Avenue, and 30th Avenue (also referred to as *Norte Quito Sur* or *N.Q.S.* for short). Routes for Suba Avenue and Southern Highway (*Autopista Sur* ), the southern leg of the 30th Avenue, were opened in April 2006. The third phase of the system will cover 7th Avenue, 10th Avenue, and 26th Street (or *Avenida El Dorado*). The system is planned to cover the entire city by 2030. Although the Transmilenio carries commuters to numerous corners of the city, it is more expensive (US$0.80 or 2300 COP) than any public transport, except taxis.{#cite_ref-99}

In addition to TransMilenio, the Peñalosa administration and voter-approved referendums helped to establish travel restrictions on cars with certain license plate numbers during peak hours called [Pico y placa](/wiki/Pico_y_placa "Pico y placa") (peak, as in hour, and plate, as in license plate); 121 kilometers (75 miles) of [Ciclovía](/wiki/Ciclov%C3%ADa "Ciclovía") on Sundays and major holidays; a massive system (376 km (234 mi) as of 2013^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit)^) of bicycle paths and segregated lanes called *[ciclorrutas](/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1%27s_Bike_Paths_Network "Bogotá's Bike Paths Network")* ; and the removal of thousands of parking spots in an attempt to make roads more pedestrian-friendly and discourage car use. *Ciclorrutas* is one of the most extensive dedicated bike path networks of any city in the world, with a total extension of 376 kilometers (234 miles). It extends from the north of the city, 170th Street, to the south, 27th Street, and from [Monserrate](/wiki/Monserrate "Monserrate") on the east to the [Bogotá River](/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_River "Bogotá River") on the west. The *ciclorruta* was started by the 1995--1998 [Antanas Mockus](/wiki/Antanas_Mockus "Antanas Mockus") administration with a few kilometers, and considerably extended afterwards with the development of a Bicycle Master Plan and the addition of paths hundreds of kilometers in extent.^[\[100\]](#cite_note-100)^ Since the construction of the *ciclorruta* bicycle use in the city has increased, and a car free week was introduced in 2014.^[\[101\]](#cite_note-greenblog-101)^{#cite_ref-greenblog_101-0}

  * [![Bi-articulated TransMilenio bus](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Articulado_de_Transmilenio_en_el_Eje_Ambiental.JPG/240px-Articulado_de_Transmilenio_en_el_Eje_Ambiental.JPG)](/wiki/File:Articulado_de_Transmilenio_en_el_Eje_Ambiental.JPG "Bi-articulated TransMilenio bus")

  * [![Urban (SITP) bus, part of the integrated public transport system](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Bogot%C3%A1_-_Bus_del_SITP_por_la_carrera_11.jpg/249px-Bogot%C3%A1_-_Bus_del_SITP_por_la_carrera_11.jpg)](/wiki/File:Bogot%C3%A1_-_Bus_del_SITP_por_la_carrera_11.jpg "Urban (SITP) bus, part of the integrated public transport system")  
  Urban (SITP) bus, part of the [integrated public transport system](/wiki/Integrated_Public_Transport_System_(Bogot%C3%A1) "Integrated Public Transport System (Bogotá)")
  * [![Bikepath in central Bogotá](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Bogot%C3%A1_-_Centro_Inernacional_Ciclorruta_cl_10.JPG/240px-Bogot%C3%A1_-_Centro_Inernacional_Ciclorruta_cl_10.JPG)](/wiki/File:Bogot%C3%A1_-_Centro_Inernacional_Ciclorruta_cl_10.JPG "Bikepath in central Bogotá")  
  Bikepath in central Bogotá
  * [![Traffic on the Northern Highway (Autopista Norte)](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Trancon_Autonorte.jpg/240px-Trancon_Autonorte.jpg)](/wiki/File:Trancon_Autonorte.jpg "Traffic on the Northern Highway (Autopista Norte)")  
  Traffic on the Northern Highway ([Autopista Norte](/wiki/Autopista_Norte "Autopista Norte"))

### Airports {#Airports}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Airports")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Aeropuerto_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG/220px-Aeropuerto_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG)](/wiki/File:Aeropuerto_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG) [El Dorado International Airport](/wiki/El_Dorado_International_Airport "El Dorado International Airport")

Bogotá's main airport is [El Dorado International Airport](/wiki/El_Dorado_International_Airport "El Dorado International Airport"), with an approximate area of 6.9 km^2^ (2.7 sq mi) located west of the city's downtown in the [Fontibón](/wiki/Fontib%C3%B3n "Fontibón") Locality. It is the second busiest airport in Latin America after [Mexico City International Airport](/wiki/Mexico_City_International_Airport "Mexico City International Airport") and it is the busiest airport in Colombia. Construction of the airport was ordered by [Gustavo Rojas Pinilla](/wiki/Gustavo_Rojas_Pinilla "Gustavo Rojas Pinilla") (19th President of Colombia) in 1955 to replace the [Aeropuerto de Techo](https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aeropuerto_de_Techo "es:Aeropuerto de Techo"). Due to its central location in Colombia and in Latin America, it is a hub for Colombia's Flagship Carrier [Avianca](/wiki/Avianca "Avianca"), [Copa Airlines Colombia](/wiki/Copa_Airlines_Colombia "Copa Airlines Colombia") and [LATAM Colombia](/wiki/LATAM_Colombia "LATAM Colombia"). It is also serviced by a number of international airlines including American, Delta, United, Air France, KLM, Turkish Airlines, JetBlue, Lufthansa, Emirates, Iberia and Air Canada. The national airport has begun to take more responsibility due to the congestion at the international airport. In response to the high demand of approximately 27 Million passengers per year,^[\[102\]](#cite_note-102)^{#cite_ref-102}

A secondary airport, [CATAM](/wiki/Military_Transport_Air_Command_(Colombian_Air_Force) "Military Transport Air Command (Colombian Air Force)"), serves as a base for Military and Police Aviation. This airport, which uses the runways of El Dorado will eventually move to Madrid, a nearby town in the region of Cundinamarca, leaving further space to expand El Dorado.^[\[103\]](#cite_note-103)^{#cite_ref-103}

[Guaymaral Airport](/wiki/Guaymaral_Airport "Guaymaral Airport") is another small airport located in the northern boundaries of Bogotá. It is used mainly for private aviation activities.  

### Urban and suburban railways {#Urban_and_suburban_railways}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Urban and suburban railways")\]  
Main articles: [Bogotá Metro](/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Metro "Bogotá Metro") and [Tramways of Bogotá](/wiki/Tramways_of_Bogot%C3%A1 "Tramways of Bogotá")  
See also: [Bogotá's Savannah Railway](/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1%27s_Savannah_Railway "Bogotá's Savannah Railway") and [RegioTram](/wiki/RegioTram "RegioTram")

Bogotá has little railway transit infrastructure, following the collapse of the tram network, although a number of plans hope to change that. The [Bogotá Metro](/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Metro "Bogotá Metro") has been pushed forward by two successive governments, and construction began in 2020 with opening planned for 2028.^[\[104\]](#cite_note-104)^ Plans to construct railways in and out of the city, replacing defunct routes, have been delayed due to the pressing need for transport within the city.^[\[105\]](#cite_note-105)^ A [tram train](/wiki/Tram_train "Tram train") line using right-of-way from the defunct Bogotá Savannah Railway, known as [RegioTram](/wiki/RegioTram "RegioTram"), will be opening in 2023.{#cite_ref-105}  

### Bicycle infrastructure {#Bicycle_infrastructure}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Bicycle infrastructure")\]  
Main article: [Bogotá's Bike Paths Network](/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1%27s_Bike_Paths_Network "Bogotá's Bike Paths Network")

Bogotá has most extensive and comprehensive network of bike paths in Colombia. Bogotá's bike paths network or Ciclorrutas de Bogotá in Spanish, designed and built during the administration of Mayors [Antanas Mockus](/wiki/Antanas_Mockus "Antanas Mockus") and [Enrique Peñalosa](/wiki/Enrique_Pe%C3%B1alosa "Enrique Peñalosa"), is also one of the most extensive in the world and the most extensive in Latin America.^[\[106\]](#cite_note-106)^ The network is integrated with the [TransMilenio](/wiki/TransMilenio "TransMilenio") bus system which has bicycle parking facilities, therefore rendering it feasible to cross the entire metropolitan area while riding a bike.{#cite_ref-106}

Bogotá implemented a healthy lifestyle program called "Ciclovía", through which principal highways are closed from 7:00 a.m. until 2:00 pm on Sundays and public holidays. Thanks to the "Ciclovía", the general population rides its bikes enjoying the city as well as exercising. In addition, cars do not circulate as heavily, so there is less pollution. Along the same lines, just during the month of December, the same activity is carried out at night; there are some special amenities and activities, such as fireworks, street theater performances, and street food vendors.

Since 4 April 2016 the [carrera 11](/w/index.php?title=Carrera_11&action=edit&redlink=1 "Carrera 11 (page does not exist)") has been reduced from four to three car lanes and a new bike lane (*ciclorruta* ) has been inaugurated.^[\[107\]](#cite_note-107)^{#cite_ref-107}  

### Tramway {#Tramway}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Tramway")\]

On 25 December 1884, the first tramway pulled by mules was inaugurated and covered the route from [Plaza de Bolívar](/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar_Square "Bolívar Square") to Chapinero,^[\[108\]](#cite_note-PorupRaub2009-108)^ and in 1892, the line connecting Plaza de Bolívar and La Sabana Station started operating. The tramway ran over wooden rails and was easily derailed, so steel rails imported from Britain were eventually installed. In 1894, a tramway car ran the Bogotá--Chapinero line every 20 minutes. ^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ The tram system eventually grew to cover most of the city and its surrounding suburbs. But during the [Bogotazo](/wiki/Bogotazo "Bogotazo") riots of 1948, the system suffered heavy damage and was forced to close. The economic effects of the [subsequent civil war](/wiki/La_Violencia "La Violencia") that followed prevented the damage from being repaired. Parts of the system continued to operate in a reduced state until 1951, when they were replaced by buses. Most of the streetcar tracks were eventually paved over, but exposed tracks can still be seen on many of the older roads of the city, especially downtown and in the [La Candelaria](/wiki/La_Candelaria,_Bogot%C3%A1 "La Candelaria, Bogotá") area, although it has been about 70 years^\[*[when?](/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items "Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers")*\]^ since any vehicles have run on them.{#cite_ref-PorupRaub2009_108-0}  

### Bogotá public transportation statistics {#Bogot.C3.A1_public_transportation_statistics}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: Bogotá public transportation statistics")\]

The average amount of time people spend commuting with public transit in Bogotá, for example to and from work, on a weekday is 97 min. 32% of public transit riders, ride for more than 2 hours every day. The average amount of time people wait at a stop or station for public transit is 20 min, while 40% of riders wait for over 20 minutes on average every day. The average distance people usually ride in a single trip with public transit is 8 km, while 16% travel for over 12 km in a single direction.^[\[109\]](#cite_note-109)^{#cite_ref-109}  

Education {#Education}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Education")\]  
Main article: [List of universities in Bogotá](/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Bogot%C3%A1 "List of universities in Bogotá")

Known as the Athens of South America,^[\[110\]](#cite_note-110)^ Bogotá has an extensive educational system of both primary and secondary schools and colleges. Due to the constant migration of people into the nation's capital, the availability of quotas for access to education offered by the State free of charge is often insufficient. The city also has a diverse system of colleges and private schools.{#cite_ref-110}

There are a number of universities, both public and private. In 2002, there were a total of 113 higher education institutions; in Bogotá there are several universities, most partially or fully accredited by the NAC (National Accreditation Council): [National University of Colombia](/wiki/National_University_of_Colombia "National University of Colombia"), [University of the Andes, Colombia](/wiki/University_of_the_Andes,_Colombia "University of the Andes, Colombia"), [District University of Bogotá](/wiki/District_University_of_Bogot%C3%A1 "District University of Bogotá"), [La Salle University, Colombia](/wiki/La_Salle_University,_Colombia "La Salle University, Colombia"), [University of La Sabana](/wiki/University_of_La_Sabana "University of La Sabana"), [Pontifical Xavierian University](/wiki/Pontifical_Xavierian_University "Pontifical Xavierian University"), [Our Lady of the Rosary University](/wiki/Our_Lady_of_the_Rosary_University "Our Lady of the Rosary University"), [Universidad Externado de Colombia](/wiki/Universidad_Externado_de_Colombia "Universidad Externado de Colombia"), [Military University Nueva Granada](/wiki/Military_University_Nueva_Granada "Military University Nueva Granada"), [Central University, Colombia](/wiki/Central_University_(Colombia) "Central University (Colombia)"), [El Bosque University](/wiki/El_Bosque_University "El Bosque University"), University of America, [Sergio Arboleda University](/wiki/Sergio_Arboleda_University "Sergio Arboleda University"), [Jorge Tadeo Lozano University](/wiki/Jorge_Tadeo_Lozano_University "Jorge Tadeo Lozano University"), [Pilot University of Colombia](/wiki/Pilot_University_of_Colombia "Pilot University of Colombia"), [Catholic University of Colombia](/wiki/Catholic_University_of_Colombia "Catholic University of Colombia"), [Saint Thomas Aquinas University](/wiki/Saint_Thomas_Aquinas_University "Saint Thomas Aquinas University") and [Universidad Pedagógica Nacional](/wiki/National_Pedagogic_University_(Colombia) "National Pedagogic University (Colombia)").

The city has a University City at the National University of Colombia campus located in the traditional sector Teusaquillo. It is the largest campus in Colombia and one of the largest in Latin America.

Culture {#Culture}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Culture")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Ciclov%C3%ADa_por_la_Carrera_S%C3%A9ptima.jpg/220px-Ciclov%C3%ADa_por_la_Carrera_S%C3%A9ptima.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ciclov%C3%ADa_por_la_Carrera_S%C3%A9ptima.jpg) [Ciclovía](/wiki/Ciclov%C3%ADa "Ciclovía") in Bogotá

Bogotá has many cultural venues including 58 museums, 62 art galleries, 150 libraries (of different types), 45 stage theaters, 75 sports and attraction parks, and over 150 national monuments.^[\[111\]](#cite_note-111)^ Many of these are renowned globally such as: [BibloRed, Bogotá's Public Libraries Network](/wiki/BibloRed "BibloRed"),^[\[50\]](#cite_note-pub113-50)^ the [Luis Ángel Arango Library](/wiki/Luis_%C3%81ngel_Arango_Library "Luis Ángel Arango Library"), the most important in the region^\[*[according to whom?](/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions "Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch")*\]^ which receives well over 6 million visitors a year;^[\[112\]](#cite_note-112)^ the [Colombian National Museum](/wiki/Colombian_National_Museum "Colombian National Museum"), one of the oldest in the Americas, dating back to 1823;^[\[113\]](#cite_note-113)^ the [Ibero-American Theater Festival](/wiki/Ibero-American_Theater_Festival "Ibero-American Theater Festival"), largest of its kind in the world, receives 2 million attendees enjoying over 450 performances across theaters and off the street;^[\[114\]](#cite_note-114)^ the [Bogotá Philharmonic](/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Philharmonic "Bogotá Philharmonic") is the most important^\[*[according to whom?](/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions "Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch")*\]^ [symphony orchestra](/wiki/Symphony_orchestra "Symphony orchestra") in Colombia, with over 100 musicians and 140 performances a year.^[\[115\]](#cite_note-115)^ The city has been a member of the [UNESCO Creative Cities Network](/wiki/Creative_Cities_Network "Creative Cities Network") in the category of music since March 2012.^[\[116\]](#cite_note-116)^ In 2007, Bogotá was named [World Book Capital](/wiki/World_Book_Capital "World Book Capital") by [UNESCO](/wiki/UNESCO "UNESCO").^[\[117\]](#cite_note-:5-117)^{#cite_ref-:5_117-0}

The Cristóbal Colón Theater, the country's oldest Opera House, opened in 1892. It is home to the National Symphony Association's major act, the [National Symphony Orchestra of Colombia](/wiki/National_Symphony_Orchestra_of_Colombia "National Symphony Orchestra of Colombia").^[\[118\]](#cite_note-118)^{#cite_ref-118}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Baile_de_campesinos.jpg/220px-Baile_de_campesinos.jpg)](/wiki/File:Baile_de_campesinos.jpg) *Dance of peasants of Bogotá savanna* , 1878, by [Ramón Torres Méndez](/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Torres_M%C3%A9ndez "Ramón Torres Méndez"). Museo de la Independencia Casa del Florero.^[\[119\]](#cite_note-119)^^[\[120\]](#cite_note-120)^

[Rock al Parque](/wiki/Rock_al_Parque "Rock al Parque") or Rock at the Park is an open air rock music festival. Recurring annually, it gathers over 320,000 music fans who can enjoy over 60 band performances for free during three days a year.^[\[121\]](#cite_note-121)^ The series have been so successful during its 15 years of operation that the city has replicated the initiative for other music genres, resulting in other recent festivals like Salsa at the Park, Hip Hop at the Park, Ballet at the Park, Opera at the Park, and Jazz at the Park.{#cite_ref-121}

[Kids' Choice Awards Colombia](/wiki/Kids%27_Choice_Awards_Colombia "Kids' Choice Awards Colombia"), are the awards given in the city by [Nickelodeon](/wiki/Nickelodeon "Nickelodeon") and the first ceremony was given in 2014 by the singer [Maluma](/wiki/Maluma_(singer) "Maluma (singer)") and in [Corferias](/wiki/Corferias "Corferias") the ceremony has been the home of shows given by artists like [Austin Mahone](/wiki/Austin_Mahone "Austin Mahone"), [Carlos Peña](/wiki/Carlos_Pe%C3%B1a "Carlos Peña")^\[*[clarification needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify "Wikipedia:Please clarify")*\]^, [Don Tetto](/wiki/Don_Tetto "Don Tetto") and [Riva](/w/index.php?title=Riva_(singer)&action=edit&redlink=1 "Riva (singer) (page does not exist)") among others.

Bogotá has worked in recent years to position itself as leader in cultural offerings in South America, and it is increasingly being recognized worldwide as a hub in the region for the development of the arts.^[\[122\]](#cite_note-122)^^[\[123\]](#cite_note-123)^^[\[124\]](#cite_note-124)^^[\[125\]](#cite_note-125)^ In 2007, Bogotá was awarded the title of Cultural Capital of [Ibero-America](/wiki/Ibero-America "Ibero-America") by the UCCI ([Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities](/wiki/Union_of_Ibero-American_Capital_Cities "Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities")), and it became the only city to have received the recognition twice, after being awarded for the first time in 1991.^[\[126\]](#cite_note-126)^{#cite_ref-126}  

### Cultural history {#Cultural_history}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: Cultural history")\]

Bogotá gave the Spanish-speaking world [José Asunción Silva](/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Asunci%C3%B3n_Silva "José Asunción Silva") (1865--1896), [Modernism](/wiki/Modernism "Modernism") pioneer. His poetic work in the novel *De sobremesa* has a place in outstanding American literature. [Rafael Pombo](/wiki/Rafael_Pombo "Rafael Pombo") (1833--1912) was an [American romanticism](/wiki/American_romanticism "American romanticism") poet who left a collection of fables essential part of children imagination and Colombian tradition.  

### Architecture {#Architecture}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: Architecture")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Construcci%C3%B3n_del_BD_Bacat%C3%A1.JPG/170px-Construcci%C3%B3n_del_BD_Bacat%C3%A1.JPG)](/wiki/File:Construcci%C3%B3n_del_BD_Bacat%C3%A1.JPG) [BD Bacatá](/wiki/BD_Bacat%C3%A1 "BD Bacatá"), under construction, will be the city's tallest building.

The urban morphology and typology of colonial buildings in Bogotá have been maintained since the late nineteenth century, long after the independence of Colombia (1810). ^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ This persistence of the colonial setting is still visible, particularly in La Candelaria, the historical center of Bogotá. Also kept up are the colonial houses of two stories, with courtyards, gabled roofs, ceramic tiles and balconies. In some cases, these balconies were enclosed with glass windows during the Republican period, a distinguishing feature of the architecture of the sector (for example, the House of Rafael Pombo).^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^

"Republican Architecture" was the style that prevailed between 1830 and 1930.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ Although there were attempts to consolidate a modern architectural language, the only examples seen are University City and White City at the National University of Colombia (constructed 1936--39). This work was developed by German architect [Leopold Rother](/wiki/Leopold_Rother "Leopold Rother"), although architects of rationalist trends participated in the design of campus buildings. There are also architecture trends such as art deco, expressionism and organic architecture. This last trend was typified by Bogotan architects in the second half of the twentieth century such as [Rogelio Salmona](/wiki/Rogelio_Salmona "Rogelio Salmona").

In 2015 [BD Bacatá](/wiki/BD_Bacat%C3%A1 "BD Bacatá") was inaugurated, surpassing the [Colpatria Tower](/wiki/Torre_Colpatria "Torre Colpatria") to become the tallest building of the city and of Colombia.^[\[127\]](#cite_note-127)^ The building its expected to be the beginning of the city's downtown renovation.{#cite_ref-127}

  * [![Santa Barbara business district](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Centro_empresarial_St_b%C3%A1rbara_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG/240px-Centro_empresarial_St_b%C3%A1rbara_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG)](/wiki/File:Centro_empresarial_St_b%C3%A1rbara_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG "Santa Barbara business district")  
  Santa Barbara business district
  * [![Victorian architecture in Teusaquillo](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Casas_en_La_Merced%2C_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG/240px-Casas_en_La_Merced%2C_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG)](/wiki/File:Casas_en_La_Merced,_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG "Victorian architecture in Teusaquillo")  
  [Victorian architecture](/wiki/Victorian_architecture "Victorian architecture") in [Teusaquillo](/wiki/Teusaquillo "Teusaquillo")
  * [![Torres del Parque](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Torres_del_parque_torre_B.JPG/240px-Torres_del_parque_torre_B.JPG)](/wiki/File:Torres_del_parque_torre_B.JPG "Torres del Parque")  
  Torres del Parque

  Santa Maria [bullring](/wiki/Bullring "Bullring")

### Libraries and archives {#Libraries_and_archives}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&section=38 "Edit section: Libraries and archives")\]

In 2007, Bogotá was named [World Book Capital](/wiki/World_Book_Capital "World Book Capital") by [UNESCO](/wiki/UNESCO "UNESCO").^[\[117\]](#cite_note-:5-117)^ Bogotá is the first Latin American city to receive this recognition, and the second one in the Americas after [Montreal](/wiki/Montreal "Montreal"). It stood out in programs, the library network and the presence of organizations that, in a coordinated manner, are working to promote books and reading in the city. Several specific initiatives for the World Book Capital program have been undertaken with the commitment of groups, both public and private, engaged in the book sector.{#cite_ref-:5_117-1}

The city is home to the [Biblored](/wiki/Biblored "Biblored"), a network which administers 146 small and four large public libraries (Biblioteca Virgilio Barco, Biblioteca El Tintal, Biblioteca El Tunal and Biblioteca Julio Mario Santodomingo).^[\[50\]](#cite_note-pub113-50)^ It also has six branches of the Library Network of the Family Compensation Fund Colsubsidio and libraries and documentation centers attached to institutions like the Museo Nacional de Colombia (specializing in old books, catalogs and art), [Bogotá Museum of Modern Art](/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Museum_of_Modern_Art "Bogotá Museum of Modern Art"), the Alliance Française, and the Centro Colombo Americano.{#cite_ref-pub113_50-2}

Another set of libraries are the new collaborative initiatives between the state, city and international agencies. Examples are the Cultural Center Gabriel García Marquez, custom designed by the Fondo de Cultura Economica in Mexico, and the Spanish Cultural Center, which will begin construction with public funds and of the Spanish government in downtown Bogotá. ^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^

The [National Library of Colombia](/wiki/National_Library_of_Colombia "National Library of Colombia") (1777), a dependence of the Ministry of Culture and the Biblioteca Luis Angel Arango (1958), a dependence of the Bank of the Republic are the two largest public libraries in the city. The first is the repository of more than two million volumes, with an important collection of ancient books. The latter has almost two million volumes, and with 45,000 m^2^ (480,000 [sq ft](/wiki/Square_foot "Square foot")) in size, it hosts 10,000 visitors a day; the Library Alfonso Palacio Rudas is also a dependence of the Bank of the Republic, and is located at the north of the city, with about 50,000 volumes. Other large public libraries are the Library of Congress in Colombia (with 100,000 volumes), of the Instituto Caro y Cuervo (with nearly 200,000 volumes, the largest Latin American library in Philology and Linguistics), the Library of the Academy of History The Library of the Academy of Language, the Library of the Colombian Institute of Anthropology and History ICANH, and many university libraries.

Bogotá is home to historical records housed in the General National Archive, a collection of about 60 million documents, one of the largest repositories of primary historical sources in Latin America. Bogotá is also home to the Musical Archive of the Cathedral of Bogotá (with thousands of books and choral song-colonial period), the Archdiocesan Archive, the Archive of the Conciliar Seminary of Bogotá, the Archive History National University of Colombia and the Archive of the Mint in Bogotá, under the Bank of the Republic.

  * [![National Library of Colombia](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Biblioteca_nacional_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG/240px-Biblioteca_nacional_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG)](/wiki/File:Biblioteca_nacional_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG "National Library of Colombia")  
  [National Library of Colombia](/wiki/National_Library_of_Colombia "National Library of Colombia")
  * [![Julio Mario Santo Domingo Public Library](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Biblioteca_Julio_Mario_Santodomingo_.jpg/320px-Biblioteca_Julio_Mario_Santodomingo_.jpg)](/wiki/File:Biblioteca_Julio_Mario_Santodomingo_.jpg "Julio Mario Santo Domingo Public Library")  
  Julio Mario Santo Domingo Public Library

  Virgilio Barco Public Library

  El Tintal Public Library

### Museums and galleries {#Museums_and_galleries}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&section=39 "Edit section: Museums and galleries")\]  
See also: [List of museums in Colombia § Bogotá and Cundinamarca](/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Colombia#Bogotá_and_Cundinamarca "List of museums in Colombia")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Fachada_museo_nacional.JPG/220px-Fachada_museo_nacional.JPG)](/wiki/File:Fachada_museo_nacional.JPG) [Colombian National Museum](/wiki/Colombian_National_Museum "Colombian National Museum")

The city offers 58 museums and over 70 art galleries. ^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ The [Colombian National Museum](/wiki/Colombian_National_Museum "Colombian National Museum") has acquisitions divided into four collections: art, history, archeology and ethnography. The [Gold Museum](/wiki/Gold_Museum,_Bogot%C3%A1 "Gold Museum, Bogotá"), with 35,000 pieces of tumbaga gold, along with 30,000 objects in ceramic, stone and textiles, represents the largest collection of pre-Columbian gold in the world.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^

The [Botero Museum](/wiki/Botero_Museum "Botero Museum") has 123 works of Fernando Botero and 87 works by international artists. The [Bogotá Museum of Modern Art](/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Museum_of_Modern_Art "Bogotá Museum of Modern Art") has a collection of graphic arts, industrial design and photography. The Museum of Colonial Art is home to an important collection of colonial art from Colombia. Fundación Gilberto Alzate Avendaño hosts activities related to the performing arts and shows temporary exhibits of art in its halls and galleries.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^

Among the scientific museums are the Archeological Museum -- Casa del Marqués de San Jorge, which has about 30 thousand pieces of pre-Columbian art, Instituto de Ciencias Naturales (UN), one of the four largest museums of natural sciences in Latin America, and the Geological Museum, which has a collection specializing in Geology and Paleontology.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^

Bogotá has historical museums like the [Jorge Eliecer Gaitan Museum](/wiki/Jorge_Eliecer_Gaitan_Museum "Jorge Eliecer Gaitan Museum"), the Museum of Independence (Museo de la Independencia), the [Quinta de Bolívar](/wiki/Quinta_de_Bol%C3%ADvar "Quinta de Bolívar") and the Casa Museo Francisco José de Caldas, as well as the headquarters of Maloka and the [Children's Museum of Bogotá](/wiki/Children%27s_Museum_of_Bogot%C3%A1 "Children's Museum of Bogotá"). New museums include the Art Deco and the Museum of Bogotá.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^

  * [![Colonial Art Museum of Bogotá](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Museo_AColonialB.jpg/240px-Museo_AColonialB.jpg)](/wiki/File:Museo_AColonialB.jpg "Colonial Art Museum of Bogotá")  
  [Colonial Art Museum of Bogotá](/w/index.php?title=Colonial_Art_Museum_of_Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&redlink=1 "Colonial Art Museum of Bogotá (page does not exist)")
  * [![Gold Museum of Bogotá](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/BOG_04_2012_Museo_de_Oro_1278.JPG/270px-BOG_04_2012_Museo_de_Oro_1278.JPG)](/wiki/File:BOG_04_2012_Museo_de_Oro_1278.JPG "Gold Museum of Bogotá")  
  [Gold Museum of Bogotá](/wiki/Gold_Museum,_Bogot%C3%A1 "Gold Museum, Bogotá")
  * [![Archaeology Museum of Pasca](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Gold_Museum%2C_Bogota_%2836145671394%29.jpg/180px-Gold_Museum%2C_Bogota_%2836145671394%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Gold_Museum,_Bogota_(36145671394).jpg "Archaeology Museum of Pasca")  
  [Archaeology Museum of Pasca](/wiki/Archaeology_Museum,_Pasca "Archaeology Museum, Pasca")
  * [![Botero Museum](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Museo_Botero%2C_Bogota_%2850077504732%29.jpg/271px-Museo_Botero%2C_Bogota_%2850077504732%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Museo_Botero,_Bogota_(50077504732).jpg "Botero Museum")  
  [Botero Museum](/wiki/Museo_Botero "Museo Botero")

### Theater and arts {#Theater_and_arts}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&section=40 "Edit section: Theater and arts")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/FITB.jpg/190px-FITB.jpg)](/wiki/File:FITB.jpg) [Ibero-American Theater Festival](/wiki/Ibero-American_Theater_Festival "Ibero-American Theater Festival") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/af/Picolontheaterj.jpg/220px-Picolontheaterj.jpg)](/wiki/File:Picolontheaterj.jpg) *[Teatro de Cristóbal Colón](/wiki/Teatro_de_Crist%C3%B3bal_Col%C3%B3n "Teatro de Cristóbal Colón")* (Christopher Columbus Theater)

Besides the [Ibero-American Theater Festival](/wiki/Ibero-American_Theater_Festival "Ibero-American Theater Festival"), the largest theater festival in the world, the city has forty-five theaters; the principal ones are the [Colon Theater](/wiki/Teatro_de_Crist%C3%B3bal_Col%C3%B3n "Teatro de Cristóbal Colón"), the newly built [Teatro Mayor Julio Mario Santo Domingo](https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biblioteca_P%C3%BAblica_Julio_Mario_Santo_Domingo "es:Biblioteca Pública Julio Mario Santo Domingo"), the National Theater with its two venues, the traditional TPB Hall, the Theater of La Candelaria, the Camarin del Carmen (over 400 years old, formerly a convent), the Colsubsidio, and a symbol of the city, the renovated [Teatro Jorge Eliecer Gaitan](https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Teatro_Jorge_Eli%C3%A9cer_Gait%C3%A1n "es:Teatro Jorge Eliécer Gaitán"), León de Greiff Auditorium (home of the Bogotá Philharmonic Orchestra), and the Open Air Theater "La Media Torta", where musical events are also held.

The Ibero-American Theater Festival, is not the only acclaimed festival. There are many other regional and local theater festivals that are celebrated and maintain the city active year-round . Amongst these is the "Alternative Theater Festival".^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^

Bogotá has its own film festival, the [Bogotá Film Festival](/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Film_Festival "Bogotá Film Festival"), and many theaters, showing both contemporary films and art cinema. Bogotá's international art fair, [ArtBo](/wiki/ArtBo "ArtBo"), takes place in October of every year and showcases thousands of works covering arts across all formats, movements, and concepts.^[\[128\]](#cite_note-128)^{#cite_ref-128}

The main cultural center of the city is the La Candelaria, historic center of the city, with a concentration of universities and museums. In 2007 Bogotá was designated the Ibero-American cultural Capital of Iberoamerica.  

### Religion {#Religion}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&section=41 "Edit section: Religion")\]

Before the [Spanish conquest](/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Muisca "Spanish conquest of the Muisca"), the beliefs of the inhabitants of Bogotá formed part of the [Muisca religion](/wiki/Muisca_religion "Muisca religion"). From the colonial period onwards, the city has been predominantly Roman Catholic. Proof of this religious tradition is the number of churches built in the historic city center. The city has been seat of the [Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Bogotá](/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Bogot%C3%A1 "Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Bogotá") since 22 March 1564. The seat of the Archbishop is the [Primatial Cathedral of Bogotá](/wiki/Primatial_Cathedral_of_Bogot%C3%A1 "Primatial Cathedral of Bogotá"); the archdiocese itself is located in new buildings in the north of the city. The city has a mosque located in the area of Chapinero called the Estambul mosque,^[\[129\]](#cite_note-129)^ a mosque being built on the Calle 80 with Cra 30 called [Abou Bakr Al-Siddiq Mosque](/wiki/Abou_Bakr_Al-Siddiq_Mosque "Abou Bakr Al-Siddiq Mosque")^[\[130\]](#cite_note-130)^ and which is the first in the city to have the traditional Islamic architecture, and an Islamic Center called Al-Qurtubi.^[\[131\]](#cite_note-131)^{#cite_ref-131}

The main [Ashkenazi](/wiki/Ashkenazi "Ashkenazi") Jewish synagogue (there are a total of 4 synagogues in Bogotá) is located on 94th street (also called State of Israel Avenue).

An Eastern Orthodox church and the San Pablo Anglican Cathedral, the mother church of the Episcopal Church in Colombia, are both located in Chapinero. The [Bogotá Colombia Temple](/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Colombia_Temple "Bogotá Colombia Temple") of [the Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints](/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints "The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints") is located in the Niza neighborhood. There are four Buddhist centers located in the north of the city. There is also a wide variety of Protestant churches in different parts of the city, including the Bogotá Baptist Chapel, the non-denominational Union Church, and the St. Matthaus Evangelical Lutheran Church which holds services in German as well as Spanish for the German-Colombian community.

  * [![Church of Our Lady of Lourdes](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Torre_central_de_la_iglesia_de_Lourdes_en_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG/240px-Torre_central_de_la_iglesia_de_Lourdes_en_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG)](/wiki/File:Torre_central_de_la_iglesia_de_Lourdes_en_Bogot%C3%A1.JPG "Church of Our Lady of Lourdes")  
  Church of Our Lady of Lourdes

  [El Lugar de Su Presencia](/wiki/El_Lugar_de_Su_Presencia "El Lugar de Su Presencia")

### Cuisine {#Cuisine}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&section=42 "Edit section: Cuisine")\]

There is a broad array of restaurants in Bogotá that serve typical and international food. Parque de la 93, Usaquén, Zona T, The [G Zone](/w/index.php?title=G_Zone&action=edit&redlink=1 "G Zone (page does not exist)"), La Macarena, La Candelaria, The parkway and the International Center are some of the main sectors where a number of international restaurants are found, ranging from Argentinian, Peruvian, Venezuelan, Brazilian, Mexican, American establishments to Arabic, Asian, French, Italian, Russian and British bistros, rotisseries, steakhouses and pubs, just to name a few. Typical dishes of Bogotá include the [ajiaco](/wiki/Ajiaco "Ajiaco"),^[\[132\]](#cite_note-132)^ a soup prepared with chicken, a variety of potatoes, corn on the cob, and *[guascas](/wiki/Galinsoga_parviflora "Galinsoga parviflora")* (an herb), usually served with sour cream and capers, and accompanied by avocado and rice.{#cite_ref-132}

[Tamales](/wiki/Tamale "Tamale") is a very traditional Bogotá dish. Colombian tamal is a paste made with rice, beef, pork and/or chicken (depending on the region), chickpea, carrot, and spices, wrapped in [plantain](/wiki/Plantain_(cooking) "Plantain (cooking)") leaves and steam-cooked.

Figs with [arequipe](/wiki/Dulce_de_leche "Dulce de leche"), strawberries with cream, *postre de natas* and *cuajada con melao* are some of the main desserts offered in the city. [Canelazo](/wiki/Canelazo "Canelazo") is a hot drink from the Altiplano prepared with [aguapanela](/wiki/Aguapanela "Aguapanela"), cinnamon and [aguardiente](/wiki/Aguardiente "Aguardiente"). Another hot beverage is the carajillo, made with coffee (tinto as it is known in Colombia) and aguardiente.

  * [![Ajiaco is one of the city's most representative dishes.](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Ajiaco.jpg/240px-Ajiaco.jpg)](/wiki/File:Ajiaco.jpg "Ajiaco is one of the city's most representative dishes.")  
  [Ajiaco](/wiki/Ajiaco "Ajiaco") is one of the city's most representative dishes.
  * [!["Chocolate santafereño" (Santafe hot chocolate), almojábana, cheese and pandequeso](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Chocolate_Especial.jpg/276px-Chocolate_Especial.jpg)](/wiki/File:Chocolate_Especial.jpg "\"Chocolate santafereño\" (Santafe hot chocolate), almojábana, cheese and pandequeso")  
  "Chocolate santafereño" (Santafe hot chocolate), [almojábana](/wiki/Almoj%C3%A1bana "Almojábana"), cheese and [pandequeso](/wiki/Pandequeso "Pandequeso")

### Parks and recreation {#Parks_and_recreation}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&section=43 "Edit section: Parks and recreation")\]

There are numerous parks in Bogotá, with facilities for concerts, plays, movies, storytellers, and other activities.

* [Simón Bolívar Park](/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar_Park "Simón Bolívar Park") is a large park regularly used to stage free concerts (such as the annual [Rock al Parque](/wiki/Rock_al_Parque "Rock al Parque") festival).
* The public [*Parque Nacional* (National Park)](/wiki/National_Park_(Bogot%C3%A1) "National Park (Bogotá)") has green spaces, ponds, games for children, foot and bicycle paths, and venues for entertainment such as public screenings of movies and concerts and events organized by the Council of Bogotá
* The [Bogotá Botanical Garden](/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Botanical_Garden "Bogotá Botanical Garden") (*Jardín Botánico de Bogotá*)
* Mundo Aventura is an [amusement park](/wiki/Amusement_park "Amusement park"), with an entry charge and charges for the different attractions. It has rides for adults and children, a [petting zoo](/wiki/Petting_zoo "Petting zoo"), and even a small track for animal races.
* [Salitre Mágico](/wiki/Salitre_M%C3%A1gico "Salitre Mágico") is another amusement park with rides and attractions. The park is near the Simón Bolívar park, where concerts are held throughout the year.
* Parque del Chicó has trees, gardens, artificial creeks and ponds, and a colonial-style house converted into a museum; [Museo del Chicó](/w/index.php?title=Museo_del_Chic%C3%B3&action=edit&redlink=1 "Museo del Chicó (page does not exist)")
* To the north of Bogotá, in the municipality of [Tocancipá](/wiki/Tocancip%C3%A1 "Tocancipá"); [Jaime Duque Park](/wiki/Jaime_Duque_Park "Jaime Duque Park") has rides, a giant map of Colombia, various exhibits, a zoo, and a big hand holding the world, symbolizing God. There is a reproduction of the [Taj Mahal](/wiki/Taj_Mahal "Taj Mahal") in the park with a collection of reproductions of famous paintings. The park is also used for large concerts, mainly electronic music.
* [Maloka](/wiki/Maloka_Museum "Maloka Museum") is an interactive science museum, in the style of similar venues around the world.
* [Tourist train](/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Savannah_Railway "Bogotá Savannah Railway") is a sightseeing train, popular with Bogotá residents, which runs to outlying towns [Zipaquirá](/wiki/Zipaquir%C3%A1 "Zipaquirá"), [Cajicá](/wiki/Cajic%C3%A1 "Cajicá") and [Nemocón](/wiki/Nemoc%C3%B3n "Nemocón") along the lines of the former [Bogotá Savannah Railway](/wiki/Bogot%C3%A1_Savannah_Railway "Bogotá Savannah Railway") on weekends. The route to Zipaquirá (known for its [salt cathedral](/wiki/Salt_Cathedral_of_Zipaquir%C3%A1 "Salt Cathedral of Zipaquirá")) is 53 kilometers (33 miles) long. Another line goes towards the north for 47 km (29 mi) and ends at [Briceño](/wiki/Brice%C3%B1o,_Boyac%C3%A1 "Briceño, Boyacá").
* The [Usaquén Park](/w/index.php?title=Usaqu%C3%A9n_Park&action=edit&redlink=1 "Usaquén Park (page does not exist)") is another of the most important parks in the city several of the best restaurants in this city are located there, is recognized to have street performers such as storytellers, magicians, jugglers, etc., and also for being one of the most decorated parks in the city during Christmas time.

Sports {#Sports}
----------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&section=44 "Edit section: Sports")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Bogot%C3%A1_Estadio.JPG/220px-Bogot%C3%A1_Estadio.JPG)](/wiki/File:Bogot%C3%A1_Estadio.JPG) [Estadio El Campín](/wiki/Estadio_El_Camp%C3%ADn "Estadio El Campín")

The District Institute for Recreation and Sport promotes recreation, sports and use of the parks in Bogotá.

[Football](/wiki/Association_football "Association football") has been declared a symbol of Bogotá, and is widely played in the city. There are three professional clubs in the city, [Santa Fe](/wiki/Club_Santa_Fe "Club Santa Fe"), [Millonarios](/wiki/Millonarios_F%C3%BAtbol_Club "Millonarios Fútbol Club"), and [La Equidad](/wiki/La_Equidad "La Equidad"). The main stadium in the city is The Campín Stadium (Estadio Nemesio Camacho El Campín) home of the local teams [Santa Fe](/wiki/Club_Santa_Fe "Club Santa Fe") and [Millonarios](/wiki/Millonarios "Millonarios"), In 2001 The Campín Stadium was the place for the [2001 Copa América](/wiki/2001_Copa_Am%C3%A9rica "2001 Copa América") final between the [Colombia national football](/wiki/Colombia "Colombia") and the [Mexico national football](/wiki/Mexico "Mexico"), with a final score 1--0 in favor of the home team, which finally obtained its first continental cup. The other soccer venue is the multi-use Techo Metropolitan Stadium which is the home of [La Equidad](/wiki/La_Equidad "La Equidad").

Other major sporting venues are the covered Coliseum El Campín, the Simón Bolívar Aquatic Complex, the Sports Palace, the El Salitre Sports Venue which includes the [Luis Carlos Galán Velodrome](/wiki/Luis_Carlos_Gal%C3%A1n_Velodrome "Luis Carlos Galán Velodrome") (which hosted the [1995 UCI Track Cycling World Championships](/wiki/1995_UCI_Track_Cycling_World_Championships "1995 UCI Track Cycling World Championships")), the El Salitre Diamond Ballpark and the [BMX](/wiki/BMX "BMX") track "Mario Andrés Soto".

Bogotá hosted the first Bolivarian Games held in 1938. The city hosted the National Games in 2004, winning the championship. It was a sub-venue Bolivarian Pan American Games. In addition, the city on the route of the Tour of Colombia.

After being a major venue city for the [2011 FIFA U-20 World Cup](/wiki/2011_FIFA_U-20_World_Cup "2011 FIFA U-20 World Cup") that was held in [Colombia](/wiki/Colombia "Colombia"), Bogotá was one of the venue cities hosting the [2016 FIFA Futsal World Cup](/wiki/2016_FIFA_Futsal_World_Cup "2016 FIFA Futsal World Cup").^[\[133\]](#cite_note-133)^{#cite_ref-133}

Symbols {#Symbols}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&section=46 "Edit section: Symbols")\]

The flag originated with the insurgency movement against the colonial authorities which began on 20 July 1810, during which the rebels wore armbands with yellow and red bands, as these colors were those of the [Spanish flag](/wiki/Flag_of_Spain "Flag of Spain") used as the flag for the New Kingdom of Granada. ^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^

On 9 October 1952, exactly 142 years after these events, decree 555 of 1952 officially adopted the patriotic armband as the flag of Bogotá.^[\[134\]](#cite_note-134)^ The flag of Cundinamarca follows the same pattern, plus a light blue tile which represents the Virgin Mary's cape.{#cite_ref-134}

The flag itself is a yellow band above a red one. The yellow denotes the gold from the earth, as well as the virtues of justice, clemency, benevolence, the so-called "mundane qualities" (defined as nobility, excellence, richness, generosity, splendor, health, steadfastness, joy and prosperity), long life, eternity, power and constancy. The red denotes the virtue of charity, as well as the qualities of bravery, nobility, values, audacity, victory, honor and furor, Colombians call it the blood of their people. ^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^

The coat of arms of the city was granted by emperor [Charles V (Charles I of Spain)](/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor "Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor") to the [New Kingdom of Granada](/wiki/New_Kingdom_of_Granada "New Kingdom of Granada"), by royal decree given in [Valladolid](/wiki/Valladolid "Valladolid"), Spain on 3 December 1548. It contains a black eagle in the center, which symbolizes steadfastness. The eagle is also a symbol of the Habsburgs, which was the ruling family of the Spanish empire at the time. The eagle is crowned with gold and holds a red pomegranate inside a golden background. The border contains olive branches with nine golden pomegranates on a blue background. The two red pomegranates symbolize audacity, and the nine golden ones represent the nine states which constituted the New Kingdom of Granada at the time. In 1932 the coat of arms was officially recognized and adopted as the symbol of Bogotá. ^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^

Bogotá's anthem lyrics were written by Pedro Medina Avendaño; the melody was composed by Roberto Pineda Duque. The song was officially declared the anthem by decree 1000 31 July 1974, by then Mayor of Bogotá, Aníbal Fernandez de Soto.

### Twin towns -- sister cities {#Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_sister_cities}

### Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities {#Union_of_Ibero-American_Capital_Cities}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Bogot%C3%A1&action=edit&section=49 "Edit section: Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities")\]

Bogotá is part of the [Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities](/wiki/Union_of_Ibero-American_Capital_Cities "Union of Ibero-American Capital Cities") established on 12 October 1982.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^
